Here are the key findings about Prometheus' SIGTERM graceful shutdown signal handling in Go:\n\n## Overview\n\nPrometheus is a standard Unix binary, so can be asked to shutdown using a SIGTERM.\n\n## Implementation Details\n\nPrometheus uses a termination handler in cmd/prometheus/main.go that sets up a channel to receive os.Interrupt and syscall.SIGTERM signals, with a signal notification mechanism that logs a warning message when receiving an OS signal and exits gracefully.\n\n## Graceful Shutdown Process\n\nThe scrape manager coordinates termination of potentially thousands of active HTTP scrapes, and must be stopped before closing the local TSDB so that it doesn't try to write samples to a closed storage.\n\nThe TSDB shutdown triggers through fanoutStorage.Close(), which coordinates multiple storage backends and ensures proper resource cleanup.\n\n## Common Issues\n\nThe search results show several GitHub issues (from 2016-2020) where users reported Prometheus taking longer than expected to shut down after receiving SIGTERM signals, particularly when running in Kubernetes with different termination grace periods.\n\nFor a deeper look at the implementation, you can examine the Prometheus source code on GitHub, particularly the `cmd/prometheus/main.go` file where the termination handler is defined.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a9439a39-eddc-4bb2-a62d-f1dcb990d88c","uuid":"5b33bb31-432e-4b5d-9753-dcbe87337fe4","tool_use_result":{"query":"prometheus/prometheus go sigterm graceful shutdown signal","results":[{"tool_use_id":"srvtoolu_01TxFvBEpk4UGaArzNh51Rh9","content":[{"title":"Prometheus hangs indefinitely when exiting gracefully · Issue #6747 · prometheus/prometheus","url":"https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/6747"},{"title":"Periodically getting SIGTERM. When a termination signal arrives, the system:\n\n1. **Stops accepting new work** - The signal triggers cancellation of the context\n2. **Waits for cleanup** - Services have time to finish essential operations\n3. **Orders shutdown sequence** - Different components shut down in a defined sequence\n\n## Shutdown Timeout Mechanism\n\nThe code includes `webTimeout` and `queryTimeout` configurations that establish maximum durations for operations. Additionally, there's a `RemoteFlushDeadline` setting that ensures remote storage systems receive final data before termination.\n\n## Cleanup Ordering\n\nThe shutdown respects a careful ordering:\n- Rule evaluators and scrapers stop collecting new data\n- Pending queries complete within their timeout window\n- Storage systems flush remaining data\n- WAL (Write-Ahead Log) operations finalize\n- HTTP servers gracefully close connections\n\nThis structured approach prevents data loss while ensuring the process terminates in reasonable time rather than hanging indefinitely."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a9439a39-eddc-4bb2-a62d-f1dcb990d88c","uuid":"b0c18ebc-73d7-4d6d-b925-a89f486ed47a","tool_use_result":{"bytes":977772,"code":200,"codeText":"OK","result":"# Signal Handling and Graceful Shutdown in Prometheus\n\nBased on the main.go file, Prometheus implements signal handling for graceful shutdown through the `oklog/run` package. Here's the implementation:\n\n```go\nfunc SetupSignalContext() context.Context {\n    close(onlyOneSignalHandler) // panics when called twice\n    \n    shutdownHandler = make(chan os.Signal, 2)\n    \n    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n    signal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)\n    go func() {\n        <-shutdownHandler\n        cancel()\n        <-shutdownHandler\n        os.Exit(1) // second signal. Exit directly.\n    }()\n    \n    return ctx\n}\n```\n\n## Key Functionality\n\n**Signal Registration**: The function uses `signal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)` to listen for SIGTERM and SIGINT signals.\n\n**Shutdown Behavior**: According to the documentation, \"a context.Context is returned\" and \"a second signal is caught, the program is terminated with exit code 1.\"\n\n**Graceful Termination**: The first signal triggers `cancel()`, initiating graceful shutdown. A second signal forces immediate exit with code 1, preventing indefinite hangs.\n\n**Single-Use Protection**: The `close(onlyOneSignalHandler)` statement ensures this function can only be called once, panicking if invoked multiple times."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a9439a39-eddc-4bb2-a62d-f1dcb990d88c","uuid":"554a3267-ea57-4b47-a7e8-9f48c0975640","tool_use_result":{"bytes":273315,"code":200,"codeText":"OK","result":"# SetupSignalContext Function and Signal Handling\n\nThe `SetupSignalContext` function in the Kubernetes apiserver package handles graceful shutdown through OS signals. The implementation uses a buffered channel with capacity of 2 to accommodate multiple signals.\n\n## Context-Based Shutdown\n\nTwo complementary functions provide signal handling:\n\n1. **SetupSignalContext()** - Returns a `context.Context` that cancels upon receiving the first signal\n2. **SetupSignalHandler()** - Wraps the context approach, returning a done channel instead\n\nAs documented: \"A stop channel is closed on one of these signals. If a second signal is caught, the program is terminated with exit code 1.\"\n\n## Cleanup Pattern\n\nThe signal goroutine implements a two-signal escalation strategy:\n\n```\nFirst signal  → calls cancel() (graceful shutdown initiation)\nSecond signal → calls os.Exit(1) (forced termination)\n```\n\n## Programmatic Shutdown\n\nThe `RequestShutdown()` function allows code to simulate receiving a shutdown signal, sending `shutdownSignals[0]` to the handler channel. When a termination signal arrives, the handler logs the event and initiates graceful shutdown. The cleanup sequence follows a specific ordering enforced by the oklog/run pattern: web handler shutdown first, followed by scrape discovery manager, notify discovery manager, rule manager, scrape manager (must precede storage closure to prevent writes to closed storage), storage/TSDB closure, and finally notifier manager. A configurable `--storage.remote.flush-deadline` (default 1 minute) provides shutdown timeout protection for flushing remote storage.\\n\\n**Kubernetes (kubernetes/kubernetes)** implements signal handling through an abstracted context-based mechanism. The function returns a `context.Context` that cancels on the first signal (graceful shutdown) or forces exit with code 1 on a second signal (forcing termination). The method accepts a context parameter for timeout control and delegates service termination to a manager adapter. While the entry point `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/main.go` appears minimal, actual signal handling uses Go's `signal.Notify()` to register `os.Interrupt`, `os.Kill`, and `syscall.SIGTERM`. Upon receiving signals, the server initiates graceful shutdown by calling `server.Shutdown()` which logs the shutdown initiation and coordinates termination of all background services through the manager adapter. The implementation respects context deadlines and logs warnings if shutdown timeout is exceeded.\\n\\nAll three projects implement the two-signal escalation pattern (first signal initiates graceful shutdown, second signal forces termination) and emphasize proper cleanup ordering to prevent data loss and resource leaks. The kube-controller-manager implements shutdown timeout handling in `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` through the `RunControllers()` function which accepts a configurable `shutdownTimeout` parameter, coordinating controller termination and cleanup through context cancellation, with proper cleanup ordering via defer statements for event broadcaster and informer factory shutdown.\\n\\n**Grafana (grafana/grafana)** implements graceful shutdown through `pkg/server/server.go` with a `Shutdown()` method that uses `sync.Once` to ensure single execution. The method accepts a context parameter for timeout control and delegates service termination to a manager adapter. While the entry point `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/main.go` appears minimal, actual signal handling uses Go's `signal.Notify()` to register `os.Interrupt`, `os.Kill`, and `syscall.SIGTERM`. Upon receiving signals, the server initiates graceful shutdown by calling `server.Shutdown()` which logs the shutdown initiation and coordinates termination of all background services through the manager adapter. The implementation respects context deadlines and logs warnings if shutdown timeout is exceeded.\\n\\nAll three projects implement the two-signal escalation pattern (first signal initiates graceful shutdown, second signal forces termination) and emphasize proper cleanup ordering to prevent data loss and resource leaks. Kubernetes uses context-based coordination for elegant signal propagation throughout the system, Prometheus uses explicit manager shutdown in defined order, and Grafana uses a centralized manager adapter for coordinating service termination.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
